<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard_logo.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="159" data-file-width="300" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Fort_Boyard_logo.png/200px-Fort_Boyard_logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/90/Fort_Boyard_logo.png 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard_logo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of <i>Fort Boyard</i> from 2010 to 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><b>Fort Boyard</b></i> is a French <a href="/wiki/Game_show" title="Game show">game show</a> created by <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Antoine" title="Jacques Antoine">Jacques Antoine</a> that was first broadcast on 7 July 1990 (originally as <i>Les Clés de Fort Boyard</i>, however shortened to <i>Fort Boyard</i> from the second series in 1991). Foreign versions of the show have aired around the world since 1990.</p>
<p>Set and filmed on the real <a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard_(fortification)" title="Fort Boyard (fortification)">fortress of the same name</a> in France, the programme appears similar to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crystal_Maze" title="The Crystal Maze">The Crystal Maze</a></i> (which was created as an alternative format by Antoine for <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> in the United Kingdom, after <i>Fort Boyard</i> itself was unavailable to film in because of its then ongoing refurbishment during 1988–89). <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Channel 5</a> later bought the rights to <i>Fort Boyard</i> and made their own British version, using the now refurbished set, which aired from 16 October 1998 to 29 December 2001 for four series. It was briefly revived by <a href="/wiki/Challenge_(TV_channel)" title="Challenge (TV channel)">Challenge</a> in 2003 for one series and the show later returned to UK television in 2012 under a new format aired on <a href="/wiki/CITV" title="CITV">CITV</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard:_Ultimate_Challenge" title="Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge">Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge</a></i>.</p>
<p>In both programmes the contestants have to complete challenges to win prize money. However, while <i>The Crystal Maze</i> varies the type of games quite considerably, <i>Fort Boyard</i> tends to focus mainly on physical and endurance challenges. Although <i>Fort Boyard</i> was something of a pioneer in the area of game show fear and adventure, later programmes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_Factor" title="Fear Factor">Fear Factor</a></i> have pushed things even further, requiring <i>Fort Boyard</i> to react and adapt with new twists and games, including a couple of seasons in which the contestants spent the night in the Fort (this was particularly popular in the French and Russian versions).</p>
<p><i>Fort Boyard</i> is the most exported French TV format and the fourth most exported adventure-style game show format in the world after <i><a href="/wiki/Wipeout_(2008_U.S._game_show)" title="Wipeout (2008 U.S. game show)">Wipeout</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_Factor" title="Fear Factor">Fear Factor</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Survivor_(TV_series)" title="Survivor (TV series)">Survivor</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_cast">UK cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: UK cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the UK, two sets of presenters have been used for <i>Fort Boyard</i>. The first set appeared during the first four series of the show, which were broadcast by <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Channel 5</a>, with the second appearing in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Challenge_(TV_channel)" title="Challenge (TV channel)">Challenge</a>-aired fifth series. The Channel 5 years were produced by Paul Kirrage and executive produced by Richard Holloway, later known for producing <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_TV_series)" title="The X Factor (UK TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> and other high-profile shows on UK television. In March 2002, it was announced that Channel 5 had cancelled the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The leading presenters of <i>Fort Boyard</i> on Channel 5 and Challenge were <a href="/wiki/Melinda_Messenger" title="Melinda Messenger">Melinda Messenger</a> (series 1–4) and Jodie Penfold (series 5). Their roles were to give advice and support for the teams, commentate for the viewers, and match wits with Boyard, the "Master of the Fort".</p>
<p>The other characters in <i>Fort Boyard</i> are:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Boyard</b> (played by <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Grantham" title="Leslie Grantham">Leslie Grantham</a> in series 1–4, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Ellison" title="Christopher Ellison">Christopher Ellison</a> in series 5) is the "<b>Master Of The Fort</b>", who sets the challenges that the team must complete to win. In the UK versions of the show, he is portrayed as a selfish, commanding, and malevolent character who takes great pleasure in ensuring that fear and failure plague the contestants. Grantham portrayed these traits slightly more strongly, with Ellison sometimes showing sympathy, or even being generous to the contestants.</li>
<li><b>The Professor</b> (<a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Bayldon" title="Geoffrey Bayldon">Geoffrey Bayldon</a>, series 1–4) is an eccentric scientist who has become mad over the years as a result of being kept prisoner by <i>Boyard</i> in the 'Watch Tower'. His task is to ask the contestants riddles, which, if answered correctly, will give the team a key or clue word. Along with <i>Captain Baker</i>, he also talks to the contestants briefly before asking the riddles and to the viewers.</li>
<li><b>Captain Baker</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Baker" title="Tom Baker">Tom Baker</a>, series 5), the replacement for <i>The Professor</i>, is an insane sea captain held captive by <i>Boyard</i>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Boyard_cast"><i>Fort Boyard</i> cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Fort Boyard cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Passe_Partout.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="667" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Passe_Partout.jpg/150px-Passe_Partout.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Passe_Partout.jpg/225px-Passe_Partout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Passe_Partout.jpg/300px-Passe_Partout.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Passe_Partout.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
André Bouchet, 2009. (Passe-Partout)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is also the resident <i>Fort Boyard</i> cast, who first appeared in the French version, and were subsequently featured in most of the other international formats, including the original UK versions, however these were all excluded for <i><a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard:_Ultimate_Challenge" title="Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge">Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge</a></i>:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Jacques</b> (1990–) and <b>Jules</b> (1990–2009) (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Bouchet" title="fr:André Bouchet">André Bouchet</a> and <a class="external text" href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm1235442/" rel="nofollow">Alain Prévost</a> respectively) are two dwarves who lead the team through the Fort to the next challenge. <b>Deni</b> (<a class="external text" href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm1658991/" rel="nofollow">Anthony Laborde</a>) later in the show replaces Jules, who retired in 2010. Deni has appeared in the foreign versions since 2000 (replacing Jules) and from 2004 in the French series. The three are called <b>Passe-Partout</b>, <b>Passe-Temps</b>, and <b>Passe-Muraille</b> respectively in the French version.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd><i>Jacques (Passe-Partout)</i> is also responsible for locking the contestants in the cells of the Fort if they fail to get out within the time limit; whilst <i>Jules (Passe-Temps)</i>, in later series, <i>Deni (Passe-Muraille)</i> takes contestants to the 'The Watch Tower'. In duel versions, Deni plays the same role of Jacques. This is because two teams are playing at the same time.</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b>Monique</b> (1991–1997, 1999–2005, 2007–) (<a class="external text" href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0029759/" rel="nofollow">Monique d`Angeon</a>) turns a statue shaped as a tiger's head to release the gold or close the gate in the 'Treasure Room'. She is called <b>Felindra</b> in the French version and was absent in 1998 and in 2006, replaced by Kareen Le Portier (Thierry's daughter).</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>In 1998, the unnamed <b>Tiger Master</b> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thierry_Le_Portier" title="fr:Thierry Le Portier">Thierry Le Portier</a>) performs this role. He is called <b>Major</b> in the French version.</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b>La Boule</b> (1994–2013) (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yves_Marchesseau" title="fr:Yves Marchesseau">Yves Marchesseau</a>, 1952–2014) sounds the "<a href="/wiki/Gong" title="Gong">gong</a>" to indicate the start and end of time and locks the contestants in cages when they fail to get out of challenge rooms in time. La Boule is a <a href="/wiki/Whaler" title="Whaler">whaler</a>, who has possibly found refuge in the Fort. He left the show in May 2014 for health reasons. Marchesseau died of <a href="/wiki/Esophageal_cancer" title="Esophageal cancer">esophageal cancer</a> and diabetes in September 2014 at the age of 62.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Since leaving Felindra, the tiger tamer, handles the sound the gong (now inside the Treasure Room) with her whip while Mister-Boo, the male wrestler, is responsible for taking the prisoners to the jails of the Fort.</dd>
</dl>
<p>As of 2014, there have been 41 characters in the French version. Most appeared in various games on the fort.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_contestants">Famous contestants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Famous contestants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_series">UK series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: UK series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 26 December 1999, a celebrity edition of <i>Fort Boyard</i> was broadcast, featuring <a href="/wiki/Gabby_Logan" title="Gabby Logan">Gabby Logan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Bruno" title="Frank Bruno">Frank Bruno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharron_Davies" title="Sharron Davies">Sharron Davies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Kane" title="Samuel Kane">Samuel Kane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glenda_McKay" title="Glenda McKay">Glenda McKay</a> as contestants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> As a one-off, the show's length was extended to 80 minutes so that the team had to get five keys (instead of four) and the code word in sixty minutes. The team won £7,910 for their nominated charity.</p>
<p>Series 3 aired two celebrity editions of <i>Fort Boyard</i> following the success of the 1999 special; broadcast on 5 January and 25 August 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> one edition featured <a href="/wiki/Rhodri_Williams" title="Rhodri Williams">Rhodri Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Rogers" title="Lisa Rogers">Lisa Rogers</a>, "Handy" <a href="/wiki/Andy_Kane" title="Andy Kane">Andy Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tricia_Penrose" title="Tricia Penrose">Tricia Penrose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Gayle" title="Phil Gayle">Phil Gayle</a> as the contestants. Rhodri was the team captain and the team won £14,350 for charity. The other featured <a href="/wiki/Anna_Walker_(television_presenter)" title="Anna Walker (television presenter)">Anna Walker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ubogu" title="Victor Ubogu">Victor Ubogu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annalise_Braakensiek" title="Annalise Braakensiek">Annalise Braakensiek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Vincent" title="Tim Vincent">Tim Vincent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Troy_Titus-Adams" title="Troy Titus-Adams">Troy Titus-Adams</a>. Anna Walker captained the team and they won £7,190 for charity.</p>
<p>Another celebrity edition aired at the end of series four (episode 14) in 2001 featuring <a href="/wiki/Sally_Gray_(television_presenter)" title="Sally Gray (television presenter)">Sally Gray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Wright_(actor)" title="Scott Wright (actor)">Scott Wright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nell_McAndrew" title="Nell McAndrew">Nell McAndrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Duffy" title="Keith Duffy">Keith Duffy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tris_Payne" title="Tris Payne">Tris Payne</a>. Sally Gray was the team captain and the team won £10,130 for charity. Episode 4 of series 4, on 13 October 2001, was a special featuring contestants from <a href="/wiki/The_Mole_(series_1)" title="The Mole (series 1)">series 1</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mole_(UK_TV_series)" title="The Mole (UK TV series)">The Mole</a></i>.</p>
<p>Celebrity editions were also broadcast during the 2003 series by <a href="/wiki/Challenge_(TV_channel)" title="Challenge (TV channel)">Challenge</a>. It featured <a href="/wiki/Doug_Williams_(wrestler)" title="Doug Williams (wrestler)">Doug Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katarina_Waters" title="Katarina Waters">Nikita</a> (now stars in <a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling" title="Total Nonstop Action Wrestling">TNA</a>), <a href="/wiki/Paul_Burchill" title="Paul Burchill">Paul Burchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Tighe" title="James Tighe">James Tighe</a>, and Sweet Saraya, all of whom were wrestling stars from British promotion <a href="/wiki/XWA_(professional_wrestling)" title="XWA (professional wrestling)">FWA</a>. Doug Williams captained the team. Other celebrities appearing in series 5 included <a href="/wiki/Tim_Vine" title="Tim Vine">Tim Vine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Phillips" title="Craig Phillips">Craig Phillips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_1_(UK)" title="Big Brother 1 (UK)"><i>Big Brother</i> 2000</a> winner. The team won £1,860 for charity, which was topped up by a further £5,000 because Tim Vine accepted a challenge to tell 10 jokes in one minute.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_series">French series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1993, teams on the French version of the show consist entirely of celebrities. These include: cyclist <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Fignon" title="Laurent Fignon">Laurent Fignon</a>, figure skating champion <a href="/wiki/Brian_Joubert" title="Brian Joubert">Brian Joubert</a> (appearing in 2004, 2007, 2008 and 2012), <a href="/wiki/Djibril_Ciss%C3%A9" title="Djibril Cissé">Djibril Cissé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Sy" title="Omar Sy">Omar Sy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Leslie_(singer)" title="Leslie (singer)">Leslie</a> (in 2002, 2003 and 2013), <a href="/wiki/Tony_Parker" title="Tony Parker">Tony Parker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eva_Longoria" title="Eva Longoria">Eva Longoria</a> in 2009, and many others. Many former/new hosts of the show have often appeared as contestants.</p>
<p>However, in 2010 the formula was dramatically changed and the squads, of four members each, did not consist of any celebrities. The "duel" format was used that year. The celebrities returned in 2011 playing for charity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_series">Other series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In most series of the Danish and Swedish versions, teams have consisted entirely of celebrities. In the 2010 and 2012 series of the Finnish version, team members were celebrities. Most (or all) episodes of the Russian series consisted of famous national singers, actors, TV presenters and sportsmen.</p>
<p>In the 2013 Canadian version, the teams consisted of 24 participants in total; 12 celebrities and 12 members of the public, divided into six teams of four equally.</p>
<p>In the Argentine version of the show, aired in 1999 and 2000, a celebrity joined the other 4 people to help them on their challenges.</p>
<p>In the Moroccan version, aired in early 2015 but filmed the previous year, 3 celebrities joined teams with 2 unknown people for the challenges. The first episode of <i>Jazirat Al Kanz</i> aired on 24 February and was watched by 6.4 million viewers, a record 59% audience share for 2MTV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Boyard_around_the_world"><i>Fort Boyard</i> around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fort Boyard around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Fort Boyard</i> is a <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> game show first broadcast in 1990; but the fort is also used by television stations from other countries in order to produce their own versions of the show. Foreign versions of the show can last between 22 and 80 minutes, depending on the country and format used. In total, 31 foreign versions of the show have broadcast around the world since 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<p>Some countries, such as Portugal and Romania, aired the original French version <a href="/wiki/Dub_localization" title="Dub localization">dubbed</a> or with <a href="/wiki/Subtitle_(captioning)" title="Subtitle (captioning)">subtitles</a> as opposed to producing their own. Azerbaijan (<a href="/wiki/Lider_TV" title="Lider TV">Lider TV</a>, 2009–2010), Czech Republic, Poland, Finland (<a href="/wiki/Yle_TV1" title="Yle TV1">Yle TV1</a> in 1993), Russia, Slovakia and Ukraine also did this before producing their own versions in later years.</p>
<p>In France, <a href="/wiki/Rerun" title="Rerun">reruns</a> of their own version have aired on <a href="/wiki/Gulli" title="Gulli">Gulli</a> (2006–2014), TV5Monde Europe, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_Outre-Mer_1re" title="Réseau Outre-Mer 1re">1ère</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France_4" title="France 4">France 4</a> since 6 September 2014.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_history">Production history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Production history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1410" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg/220px-Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg/330px-Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg/440px-Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard_States_play.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
International versions of <i>Fort Boyard</i> (map correct as of 2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fort_Boyard.jpeg/220px-Fort_Boyard.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fort_Boyard.jpeg/330px-Fort_Boyard.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fort_Boyard.jpeg/440px-Fort_Boyard.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Boyard.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard_(fortification)" title="Fort Boyard (fortification)">Fort Boyard</a>, as seen from the sea.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Each year, several episodes are recorded from May to July (or August in 2000; due to a large number of countries attending) for various television networks around the world, mostly in Europe.</p>
<p>Italy have only ever made a <a href="/wiki/Television_pilot" title="Television pilot">pilot</a> for <i>Fort Boyard</i>, in 1991. In October 2010, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> had signed on for 2011. However, no series was later produced for either country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> A Chinese version of the show was confirmed to be filmed in mid-September 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> however it was later cancelled due to <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> worries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Returns_to_the_fort">Returns to the fort</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Returns to the fort">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The United Kingdom, Norway and Sweden returned in 2011 to film new series' of the show. That same year, the Netherlands also returned after a 20-year absence. These have all adapted to the new "duel" version.</p>
<p>Finland and Russia returned in 2012, after a break of one and five years respectively. Canada returned to the fort in 2013, after an absence of 12 years since the last season was recorded in 2000 (broadcast in 2001) and produced their first "duel" version of the show.</p>
<p>Belgium, Denmark &amp; Germany returned in recent years for a new series, but have not since 2011. Armenia and Bulgaria (as a solo nation) in 2009, Finland in 2010, Azerbaijan in 2013, Morocco in 2014 and the Czech Republic in 2016, joined to produce their own versions. Bulgaria previously took part in a Balkans tri-nations version during 2007 &amp; 2008, with former participant Turkey (who last filmed a single-team version in 2000).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Figures">Figures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Figures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Currently, the year 2000 contains the most episodes filmed of any year (123 for eleven countries). To date, 2005 has the least (26), with just the French and Greek versions attending.</p>
<p>Here are the numbers (French version included):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-5" style="-moz-column-count: 5; -webkit-column-count: 5; column-count: 5;">
<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li>1990: 40</li>
<li>1991: 37</li>
<li>1992: 32</li>
<li>1993: 54</li>
<li>1994: 64</li>
<li>1995: 76</li>
<li>1996: 76</li>
<li>1997: 57</li>
<li>1998: 59</li>
<li>1999: 115</li>
<li>2000: 123</li>
<li>2001: 45</li>
<li>2002: 35</li>
<li>2003: 100</li>
<li>2004: 81</li>
<li>2005: 26</li>
<li>2006: 72</li>
<li>2007: 61</li>
<li>2008: 78</li>
<li>2009: 52</li>
<li>2010: 71</li>
<li>2011: 84</li>
<li>2012: 64</li>
<li>2013: 53</li>
<li>2014: 71</li>
<li>2015: 32</li>
<li>2016: 42</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>Overall number of episodes filmed since 1990 = <big><b>1,689</b></big> (at the end of 2016 filming)</li>
<li>Overall number of French episodes filmed = <b>207</b> (in 27 seasons)</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Productions_for_2014">Productions for 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Productions for 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Did not return in 2015:</p>
<dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Fort Boyard</i>’s format varies from country to country, but the basics are the same. A team of friends enter the Fort with the intention of winning Boyard’s gold. To do this, the contestants have to successfully complete a series of challenges set by Boyard himself.</p>
<p>The first thing done in the game is the sounding of the Fort’s <a href="/wiki/Gong" title="Gong">gong</a> by French character ‘La Boule’. Once the gong sounds the game time begins ticking down. In the UK version the game lasted for 40 minutes, in the French version 60 to 120 minutes, depending on the year. As of 2013, most countries use the show's new "duel" version, except the French.</p>
<p>The show's original format is outlined in the following sections, starting with 'Phase One'.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_One">Phase One</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Phase One">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first set of challenges the contestants have to complete is to win a certain number of <a href="/wiki/Key_(lock)" title="Key (lock)">keys</a> (in series 1–4 of the UK version four keys were needed, whereas five were need in series 5; five were needed in the Canadian version, and seven in the Swedish and Danish versions. The current French version requires 9 keys). These keys, once won, are used to open the <a href="/wiki/Gate" title="Gate">gate</a> to the Treasure Room, a central room in the Fort where the gold is held.</p>
<p>The challenges that are set to win the keys are located in small cells around the Fort, with small water-timers (a <a href="/wiki/Water_clock" title="Water clock">Clepsydre</a>) outside to give the contestant a time limit (around 2–3 minutes, depending on the game) to complete it; in the UK version, Boyard would start the timer upon saying to a contestant that "their time starts now", whereas in the 5th series, Boyard would start it after telling Jacques to open the door of a challenge room. If a contestant fails to leave the challenge room before the time runs out, he or she is locked in and then shortly after taken away to a cage (by La Boule) meaning they are not allowed to continue with the rest of the key games and must stay there until then end of <i>Phase One</i>. In the UK's 4th series, La Boule would give the contestant a large bunch of rusty keys. One of these keys would unlock the cage allowing the contestant to re-join the team.</p>
<p>During this phase of the game, one contestant goes up to the Watch Tower to win an additional key for the team (see <a href="#The_Watch_Tower">below</a>). This could be done twice.</p>
<p>Once the contestants reach the end of Phase One, usually towards the end of their game time, there is a trip to the Treasure Room with all of the keys that they have won so far. If they have enough to unlock the Treasure Room Door then the keys are entered and the gate is unlocked. However, it does not open until later in the show.</p>
<p>If they are short of keys to open the gate then team members are 'sacrificed' for keys, one team member for each key short. The 'sacrificed' contestants are then placed in an underground cell and locked in. These team members remain for the rest of the game, and are therefore unable to contribute any more for the team. Although this never happened, hypothetically at least in Series 5 in the UK, if no keys were won in Phase One, it would have been impossible for the team to continue the game since in Series 5 in the UK five keys were needed to open the treasure room door, and since there are only 5 contestants, and no one is allowed to swim for the Captain's keys, every contestant would have to make a sacrifice for all five keys leaving no contestants spare to get clue words to workout the code word and release the gold.</p>
<p>In the recent seasons of the French version, if a team is short of keys then team members could be 'sacrificed' by facing "Judgment" <i>(Le Jugement)</i>, hosted by the character Blanche. In Judgment, each sacrificed team member would have to complete a challenge set by Blanche. If the sacrificed team member was successful in his/her challenge, Blanche would grant him/her their freedom and would be able to rejoin the team. However, if the team member fails the challenge, he/she would be sent to prison.</p>
<p>If the team has more keys than necessary to unlock the gate then any extra keys gained can be swapped for free clue words to assist the team in the next phase of the game.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_One_challenges">Phase One challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Phase One challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1990 to 2014, there were 185 different events (key games).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The name of the game may change, but the game itself usually remains the same; where possible, this list will use the names from <i>Ultimate Challenge</i>.</p>
<p>Note: This is NOT the full list of games that have been played. The years below are for when the game was played or last present at the fort, in the French version or <i>Ultimate Challenge</i> (some games are present but not played every year). A full list of games can be found here.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Here is a selection of some of these challenges:</p>
<table class="wikitable collapsible" width='80%;"'>
<tr>
<th colspan="6">List of selected games</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>No.</th>
<th width="100">Cell No.</th>
<th width="100">Name (in France)</th>
<th width="100">Year(s)</th>
<th>Information</th>
<th width="95">Status</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1</td>
<td>212 (1990–2002)<br/>
116 (2006–07)</td>
<td>Arm Wrestling (Bras de fer)</td>
<td>1990–2002,<br/>
2006–07</td>
<td>The contestant has to arm wrestle against the strongman, whilst trying to grab the key, which is in a little box, with the other hand. Between their hands is a lever, so as the contestant pushes the strongman's arm down, the key is lowered so it becomes accessible to grab.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2003, 2008)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2</td>
<td>113</td>
<td>Asylum (Asile)</td>
<td>2001–2006</td>
<td>Upon entry, the contestant notes that the key is trapped in a metal shaft. He or she then pulls a lever, which raises the key on this axis, but the lever moves to the other side of the partition that separates the cell into two. The contestant must then pass to the other side of this through a padded door rocker, the latter operating in the strength of the shoulders by throwing themeselves on the top to push it over. Once on the other side, he or she can once again operate the lever, which will again raise the key further. After several trips, the key is released from its axis and the contestant can finally collect the key and exit the cell.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2007)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3</td>
<td>202 (balcony)</td>
<td>Balancing Brollies (Parapluies)</td>
<td>2013–</td>
<td>In this event, the contestant must walk a very narrow airway strap placed across the width of the courtyard and above the Treasury Room. It starts from the balcony of the 212 cell and progresses on the strap holding two umbrellas for balance. The two umbrellas are themselves held by cables. The goal is to get a portfolio at the end of the strap. When this first action is made, the contestant must do the opposite and return to its starting point. When returned, he/she must open the wallet with a clip, since it is closed with a wire. Then it remains for him/her to open it and send the code to the team, to open the lock of the safe containing the key.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4</td>
<td>114</td>
<td>Ball Surfing (Aiguilleur)</td>
<td>1998–2002</td>
<td>To release the key the contestant has to get one ball into the bucket at the end of the runway, four sections of which are not in position. Contestants stand on a surfboard, which swivels these sections, but if they don't move quickly enough to line up the next section in time, the ball drops to the ground, so they have to start again.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2003)</td>

<tr>
<td>5</td>
<td>207</td>
<td>Barrel (Barillet)</td>
<td>2006–2010</td>
<td>To reach the door of the safe containing the key, contestants are required to move through two partitions using a giant barrel. These partitions have the fingerprints of the barrel. Contestants must have the barrel and insert it into the wall. But the cylinder has three sets of rods. So it must be run each time to find the right position to move it into the wall. After passing through the two walls, the door is safe to be opened with the same barrel and the same technique as for partitions. If they can open the door, they can get the key and exit the cell, going back through the walls, but without the barrel.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2011)</td>

<td>Barrel Maze (Débarras)</td>
<td>1999–2004</td>
<td>The player must move a barrel from one end of a maze to the other where the key is locked in a vice. On the barrel is a tool which releases the key. The maze consists of 20 barrels, including one that cannot move, and these barrels must be moved so that the key can be freed.</td>

<td>7</td>
<td>111 (2002–07)<br/>
102 (2008–10)</td>
<td>Barrel Walk (Tonneau)</td>
<td>2002–2010</td>
<td>The contestant enters a cell decorated like a wine cellar. The key is at the bottom of the cell, hanging from the ceiling. To get it, the contestant must pass through the cell while walking on a barrel lying on the ground and keeping balance by using a rope attached to a ceiling track. If he or she loses control of the barrel, the contestant can drop from the rope and put the barrel in the right direction, but doing this means the rope will reset back to the beginning of the track. Obstacles on the ground include bottle caps and large ropes. Also, a metal curled wire runs across the cell, near the end of the track, to make the game more difficult. Contestants have sometimes injured themselves when jumping from the barrel to reach the key hanging above.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2011)</td>

<td>Mousetrap (Souricière)</td>
<td>2001–2005</td>
<td>Two candidates enter the cell, a man and a woman usually. They are left with a mousetrap. The one contestant sits in the cage of the trap while the other will raise the cage using arm strength. To raise the cage, the contestant must remove a plug on one side of the trap so that his/her teammate can elevate the cage up a notch. To lock the cage, he or she only has to insert the plug into the new hole. This is than repeated on the other side of the cage. By doing this, the cage will rise gradually. Once at the top of the mousetrap, the contestant can pass their hand through the cage (which contains rats/mice in some versions) to unhook the key. To exit, he or she can exit through a door at the top with some help. But if the cage is not brought to the top before the end of the hourglass, the contestant can not exit and will remain a prisoner inside the mousetrap.</td>

To complicate the task, the cabin fills with water throughout and eels can get out from opening some pipes to come swim around. <td>2007–</td>

The contestant must hit a punching bag, in order to hit the target behind and must keep up with the treadmill. With the more punches the target receives, the key will come down lower and lower until it's released and can be collected. The contestant must be careful not to get hit in his face by the punching bag.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>47</td>
<td>221</td>
<td>Pyramid (Sacs)</td>
<td>2007–</td>
<td>In the center of the cell is a pole placed on a pyramid base. The pyramid is filled with weighted bags connected to the pole, which also lies the key underneath them. To remove the key, the contestant has to climb the pyramid and remove each bag one at a time in order. The key is also attached to the pole.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>48</td>
<td>113</td>
<td>Red Alert (Alerte rouge)</td>
<td>2012–</td>
<td>The contestant has to traverse a corridor of red wires without touching them to retrieve a key at the end. The key is located on a stand protected by glass box, which lowers each time a wire is touched. If the wires are triggered, the key becomes more and more inaccessible and, ultimately, can cause the player to be locked in (a gate at the entrance will shut if the wires are triggered five times or more). Once the contestant has the key, they can exit the cell via a different corridor running alongside (marked "Exit"). However, in 2013, the corridor was removed and the contestant will now have to go back the way they came once they retrieve the key. This test is a modern version of Topkapi, present on the fort between 1990–1993.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>

2011–15</td>
<td>This challenge manifested itself in two incarnations. In 2011, it consisted of a contestant having to guide a container containing the key along a rope through obstacles in a violently shaking room; in 1997 and 2012, however, the contestant must instead search for the key in the cabin.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed (1998, 2016)</td>

<td>50</td>

205 (2012–)</td>
<td>(Horloge de la chapelle)<br/>
Rocket Launcher (De la Terre à la Lune)</td>
<td>1990–1995,<br/>
2012–</td>
<td>In the cell, the player is on the bottom of an inclined track on which a roller shell is located. At the other end, on the top, is a pendulum movement. It is on this clock is the key. Before it can be recovered, the player must launch the shell up the pendulum. But the shell is very heavy and there is a relatively small area for momentum. In addition, the clock is always moving, so you launch the projectile at the right moment. Hit the nose of the shell to the hole in the clock, the key is then released and falls down near the player who can retrieve it and exit the cell.</td>

The contestant must go to the bottom of the cargo net, find the sheet of paper, and then find the corresponding cotton bale which may contain either another destination or the key. However, once the contestant enters the room, a gate locks shut behind them that can only be unlocked with the key; if the contestant does not acquire the key and exit the cell within the time limit, they are automatically locked in. The challenge was done with the rules of the red hourglass in French 2003 version (beyond the time of the hourglass, the contestant is not a prisoner but time is deducted from the overall timer).</td>

1998,<br/>

<td>This test is probably one of the games that has generated the most prisoners, due to its extreme difficulty. A wall stands the length of the cell. On this wall is a ledge halfway up to about 2 cm wide. The contestant must move forward on this ledge, using the ceiling to help them, to retrieve the key that is at the end of it. Once the key is recovered, he or she must come back the same way, taking care not to fall from the ledge and risk getting locked in. If the contestant falls from the ledge it is near impossible to exit the cell. In 1998, a variation of the game was made so the contestant could easily exit the cell. A two player version was also created in 2005, but removed in 2006 when the original game returned in the same cell (112).</td>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Games_for_2012">New Games for 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: New Games for 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Games_for_2013">New Games for 2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: New Games for 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Cuisine de Willy</b> (cell 215A) – First time this cell has been used since 1991. A new character, an Italian Chef, played by <a href="/wiki/Willy_Rovelli" title="Willy Rovelli">Willy Rovelli</a> (a contestant in 2012) appears in the fort's kitchen. This cell is not used in international versions and is covered up.</li>
<li><b>Père Fouras Show</b> (cell 215B) – Replaced the Code Braille in French version, known as <i>Creature Code</i> in <i>Ultimate Challenge</i>. In the international versions, Creature Code is still present on the fort.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note: Some clue games are also played as key games and vice versa.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_Two">Phase Two</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Phase Two">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Once again in this part of the game the contestants have to complete a series of challenges, but instead of playing for keys they are playing for clue words. In addition, these games are more physically and mentally challenging to the contestants than those played in <i>Phase One</i>. Before these challenges, one contestant goes to the <a href="#The_Watch_Tower">Watch Tower</a> to try to win a clue word. <i>Phase Two</i> is around 10–20 minutes long in the UK version, this depends on how long the team take to win the required amount of keys needed to open the <a href="#The_Treasure_Room">Treasure Room</a> gate.</p>
<p>The objective in this phase is to try to figure out the <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">password</a>, which, if answered correctly, will release the gold. To do this, they must try to win clue words to help them in working out the password.</p>
<p>These clue words can be placed either before or after the password to make a common phrase. For example: if the clues words were <i>hall</i> and <i>line</i> then the password would be <i>dance</i>, as in <i>dance hall</i> and <i>line dance</i>.</p>
<p>To make it even more difficult to get the clue word, a time limit (3 minutes usually; occasionally between 2:00–3:30 minutes) is placed on each game. The clue words are usually written on pieces of paper and kept in canisters filled with <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a>, and if the contestant fails to reach the canister in the allotted time the clue word explodes and the contestant loses the challenge. Unlike the First Phase, players are not locked in a cage if they fail to win the clue word.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_Two_challenges">Phase Two challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Phase Two challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1991 to 2011, there were 71 different adventures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> This section details some of <i>Fort Boyard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s most famous games. The name of the game may change from country-country; but the game itself remains the same (like in Phase One, where possible, names from <i>Ultimate Challenge</i> will be used). The years below are for when the game was played or last present at the fort, in the French version or <i>Ultimate Challenge</i>.</p>
<p>Examples of the clue games, also known as "ordeals" or "adventures", are:</p>
<table class="wikitable collapsible" width='80%;"'>
<tr>
<th colspan="5">List of selected games</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>#</th>
<th width="100">Name (in France)</th>
<th width="100">Year(s)</th>
<th>Information</th>
<th width="95">Status</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1</td>
<td>Balloon Breaker (Rocket-man)</td>
<td>2006–</td>
<td>A contestant is harnessed to the inner walls of the fort. The rest of the team must pull the rope attached to the contestant all the way down to the ground and release it sending the one in the harness flying upwards. Meanwhile, they have to break a balloon containing the number code using a stick given before the challenge. This number code must be used to unlock the box containing the clue scroll.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2</td>
<td>The Catapult (Catapulte)</td>
<td>1995–2004,<br/>
2012–</td>
<td>In the centre of the Fort sits the contestant, attached to bungee cords. Another member of the team stands with an axe, while the rest of the team turns a wheel which takes the strain of the bungee. The person with the axe then has to cut the rope, which catapults the contestant up into the air. The contestant has to look out for the clue word, which is written on a large blackboard somewhere on the top of the Fort. Since 2003, instead of a clue word, the contestant has to look out for a 4 digit code, which is written on a large blackboard somewhere on the top of the Fort. The team then have to unlock a box with the code in order to get the clue canister. This game was replaced with <i>Balloon Breaker</i> in 2006. The game returned in the 2012 Halloween Special. The game is similar, but the contestant is launched by a detonator pressed by another member of the team.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3</td>
<td>Caterpillar (Chenille)</td>
<td>2001–2006,<br/>
2011–</td>
<td>Two parallel cables are strung above the 'Treasure Room' at the same location as the <i>Tight Rope</i> game. The contestant(s) are roped and use boards to transport themselves to the centre to reach the suspended key or canister hanging from above. In the duel format, the contestant(s) must then return to their platform, unscrew the canister using a tool and read out the code for the key box.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4</td>
<td>Chain Pulley (Surplomb)</td>
<td>1996–1999</td>
<td>The contestant moves along a traverse using a chain pulley. In turn they reach three keys, which they must collect. Every time they take a key, one of the chains holding them up collapses, so that by the end they are hanging vertically. Once at the end of the traverse, they have to open a box with one of the keys, and get the clue.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed (2000)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>5</td>
<td>Clockwork (Culbuto)</td>
<td>2000</td>
<td>The contestant is strapped into a frame which is attached to a giant clockwork mechanism. When they squeeze the top of the frame, it spins around, and traverses downwards. The contestant has to spin down to a key, pick it up and throw it down to their team mates who open a safe which contains the clue word.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed (2000)</td>

<tr>
<td>6</td>
<td>The Darkness (Labyrinthe obscur)</td>
<td>1991–2001</td>
<td>The player must go through a series of chambers, which are in complete darkness, and follow a string and the other players' directions (with the use of a map) to reach the end. Along the way, the contestant goes through some water, coal, a skeleton, and such features to eventually meet a room filled with light by a flame held by a naked person of the gender opposite to the player. The clue is written somewhere on the person's body, but some players miss the word due to the multiple tattoo-like prints also on the body. Although the genitals were never in view, when <i>Fort Boyard</i> was aired before the <a href="/wiki/Watershed_(broadcasting)" title="Watershed (broadcasting)">watershed</a>, the topless woman's breasts would sometimes be blurred.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>

2006,<br/>
2012–</td>

<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>8</td>
<td>Fireman's Climb (Balancier)</td>
<td>1999–2002</td>
<td>In this game the contestant has to traverse the overhead ladder to reach the key or cartridge which is at the other end. As they get further out, their weight pulls the ladder down. The game was last played in the French version in 2002, however the equipment was still on the fort until 2007 before being used for a new game from 2008 to 2010, <i>Beam on the sea</i> (<i>Poutre à la mer</i>).</td>

<td>9</td>
<td>The Hammock (Hamac)</td>
<td>2004</td>
<td>The chosen contestant attempts to climb down a hammock to reach the clue, but climbing down the hammock destabilizes it and causes it to twist and swing even further. This challenge appeared only once.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2005)</td>

<tr>
<td>10</td>
<td>Human Bell (Cloche)</td>
<td>1999–</td>
<td>One person is strapped into the Fort’s giant swing, which is hung at a right angle to the inside Fort wall. The rest of the team pulls on a heavy rope, which moves the swing back and forth. The clue is hanging so that the swing must be horizontal in order for the contestant to grab it. The person in the swing seat has no control, so even if they want to stop, they can't unless their team lets them.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>11</td>
<td>Human Catapult (Saut intérieur)</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>The contestant stands at the top of the Fort, looking down into the centre. He or she must then jump off the platform, and grab the canister which contains the clue while bouncing back up again. Some contestants failed to pluck the courage to make the jump, in which case, the clue is automatically lost.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>12</td>
<td>Ladder Race (Échelle spéléo)</td>
<td>1994–</td>
<td>This game is suspended from the bridge of the <i>Human Catapult</i> game (see below). The contestant has to climb up a thin metal <a href="/wiki/Ladder" title="Ladder">ladder</a> in order to get the cartridge or key hanging from above. His or her team will help to achieve this, by holding the ladder down (which starts at 2 meters 50 off the ground), which is too flexible and mobile to climb alone. The game can also be played as a duel and has featured in many versions.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>13</td>
<td>Leap of Faith (Saut extérieur)</td>
<td>1996–</td>
<td>The contestant has to do a <a href="/wiki/Bungee_jumping" title="Bungee jumping">bungee jump</a> off the side of the Fort. After jumping, while hanging upside down, the player has to climb partway up the rope and undo the canister which contains the clue word. Cowardice will automatically cost the clue.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>14</td>
<td>Ocean Plunge (Tyrolienne)</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>Two contestants, one male and one female, <a href="/wiki/Zip-line" title="Zip-line">zip-line</a> down from the top of the Fort's <a href="/wiki/Bastion" title="Bastion">bastions</a> into the sea. One of them, usually the female, then swims to the <a href="/wiki/Pontoon_(boat)" title="Pontoon (boat)">pontoon</a>, whilst the other has to swim over to a <a href="/wiki/Buoy" title="Buoy">buoy</a>, where he dives down deep to reach the <a href="/wiki/Lobster_trap" title="Lobster trap">lobster pot</a>. Once he has it, he swims over to the pontoon where the second contestant opens the lobster pot, takes out a key and opens a box which contains the clue word. Once they have it they shout it out to their team using a <a href="/wiki/Megaphone" title="Megaphone">megaphone</a>. There have been a few variations to this, where the second player swims to a boat as opposed to the lobster pot. Once there, one of the pair needs to climb a ladder to reach the numbers for the other person to shout back to their team for the clue. An alternate version of this, named <i>Raging Sea</i>, is also played.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>15</td>
<td>Poles Apart (Ascension du poteau)</td>
<td>2003–2010,<br/>
2012–</td>
<td>A wooden pole is outside the Fort, above the sea, starting at cell 119 up to the terrace. The contestant must climb the pole to retrieve the canister/key at the top of it. Team members located at the cell window 219 or the terrace throw down small blocks, which the climber uses in order to move up the pole to reach the top. If the team run out of blocks, the climber is unable to reach the top and can not collect the canister or key. This game can also be played as a duel.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>16</td>
<td>Rapid Ascent (Varappe)</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>The contestant(s) must climb up the side of the fort using only the rocks on the wall face. It is usually very windy and very difficult. This game can also be played as a duel.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>17</td>
<td>Sailing (Esquif)</td>
<td>1997–2006</td>
<td>The contestant finds himself in a skiff (a kind of <a href="/wiki/Kayak" title="Kayak">kayak</a>) on the stairs outside the Fort. The rope drops, he descends the stairs and enters into the sea where there are three baskets. Once collected and attached to the rope, his teammates pull them back in. The team can then open the <a href="/wiki/Safe" title="Safe">safe</a> containing the clue, using the three small keys found inside the baskets. The keys are the same, but only one key works in each <a href="/wiki/Lock_(security_device)" title="Lock (security device)">lock</a> of the safe.</td>
<td style="background: silver">Removed<br/>
(2007)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>18</td>
<td>The Searching Head (Tête chercheuse)</td>
<td>1996–</td>
<td>The contestant moves along through a series of small chambers, with only the head exposed. In each chamber is a word which the player has to shout out to the team, who cross it off a list of similar words. The one left is the clue word. Each chamber is filled with a number of creatures to scare the player, which are in order: <a href="/wiki/Frog" title="Frog">frogs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phasmatodea" title="Phasmatodea">stick-insects</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">rats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cockroach" title="Cockroach">cockroaches</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fly" title="Fly">flies</a>.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>19</td>
<td>Sky Bike (Cablocypède)</td>
<td>1998–</td>
<td>Cycling along on the upside-down bicycle, the contestant comes to three rolled up <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">flags</a>. When unrolled each displays a letter, which the rest of the team must key into a combination lock to open a safe and gain the clue.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>20</td>
<td>Snake Pit (Serpents)</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>A contestant is lowered into the snake pit, via a ladder. The clue word is split in two, each half being written on a snake. The contestant must find the two halves to make a whole, and to do so they have to pick up each snake and check its belly to see if one of the two halves of the clue is on it. There are hundreds of them, but the clue is always written on the big ones, one half usually being in a <a href="/wiki/Barrel" title="Barrel">barrel</a> and the other half in one of the small cupboards at the side of the pit. Cowardice will forfeit the clue.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>21</td>
<td>Spiders and Scorpions (Araignées et scorpions)</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>A contestant enters a room filled with tarantulas and scorpions in a chest. Three of the arachnids hold slips of paper, but only one of them has a clue word on it. In 2011, during the French version, the game was replaced by <i>Stretcher</i>. In 2015, the game returned to the French version as the <i>Doll House</i> (<i>Maison des poupées</i>). However, in the international versions, Abandoned Cabin is replaced with the original <i>Spiders and Scorpions</i> design (now located in a smaller cell nearby). Both <i>Stretcher</i> and <i>Spiders and Scorpions</i> are played in some versions.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>22</td>
<td>Sunken House/Underwater Dome</td>
<td>1991–</td>
<td>The contestant climbs down a hole into a series of flooded <a href="/wiki/Basement" title="Basement">cellars</a>. He or she exits the first two chambers underwater, and then climbs a ladder and crawls along a low corridor, on the floor of which is a word written in sand. This word is washed away by a torrent of water after a few seconds. The contestant climbs down another ladder into another chamber, where underwater are a series of boxes. One box has the sand word on it, and in here is the clue. The player then has to swim out via an underwater corridor. From the fourth series (2001), the contestant instead has to guide a spanner tied to a chain/illuminated cable through obstacles in the flooded cellars to a bolted cylinder, which the player must open to reach the clue.</td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>23</td>
<td>Tiger Buggy (Cage aux tigres)</td>
<td>1997–</td>
<td>The contestant is sat in a buggy which they have to pedal round the Treasure Room. On the floor are two keys, which they need to collect to open a small box inside the buggy which contains the clue word. In series 3, the contestant now has to collect just one canister which contains the code to a safe, which the rest of the team opens to gain the clue. Three versions of the game have been used: 1997, 1998–2013 and from 2014 as <i>Safari</i></td>
<td style="background: lime">Present</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>24</td>
<td>Tight Rope (Funambule)</td>
<td>1997–</td>
<td>The contestant has to walk from one end of the <a href="/wiki/Tightrope_walking" title="Tightrope walking">tightrope</a> to the other where the clue hangs in a canister.</td>
<td style="background: yellow">Present in foreign versions</td>
</tr>
</table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Watch_Tower">The Watch Tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: The Watch Tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1422" data-file-width="1896" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG/220px-Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG/330px-Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG/440px-Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vigie_fort_boyard2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Watch Tower in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <i>Watch Tower</i> of the Fort lives a usually <a href="/wiki/Eccentricity_(behavior)" title="Eccentricity (behavior)">eccentric</a> character that sets riddles for certain contestants; if the contestants give the correct answer, they receive a key. In the case of the clue riddles, the answer to the riddle is the clue word, so even if the contestant doesn't solve it in the <i>Watch Tower</i> he or she can still think about it during the rest of the game. If the contestant gives an incorrect answer to a key riddle, the key is "thrown" in to the sea, and another contestant has to swim for it. This was always won as the strongest swimmer would retrieve the key. The swim was removed in series 5 of the UK version, but was re-introduced in <i>Ultimate Challenge</i> as <b>Key to the Sea</b> (without the <i>Watch Tower</i> riddle).</p>
<p>Since 2006, the contestants can no longer swim for the key; it is just put back where it was held. The clue word is also different and is not the same as the riddle. Therefore, the riddle must be solved within the time limit to obtain the clue.</p>
<p>In the French version from 2011 to 2013, <i>The Watch Tower</i> wasn't used; instead, there were three trips to the <b>Interactive Cell</b>. The second trip was a <b>Visual Riddle</b>, about halfway through the key games, with Father Fouras on screen. The Clue Riddle is replaced by a telephone riddle where the player is in a booth inside one of the cells and has 1 minute to solve the riddle, given by Father Fouras over the phone, whilst cockroaches are dropped on top of them. This takes form of a game, called <b>Abandoned Cabin</b>, in the French version. <i>The Watch Tower</i> was however used in the 2012 Russian version of the show (the only country to use it that year) and in 2013 for the Azerbaijan, Canadian and Swedish versions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Treasure_Room">The Treasure Room</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: The Treasure Room">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Treasure Room (or Treasure Chamber in <i>Ultimate Challenge</i>) is the climax to each episode of <i>Fort Boyard</i>. The gold is stored here, which is guarded by Boyard's tigers (except in <i>Ultimate Challenge</i> until 2013).</p>
<p>Once the Fort’s gong sounds for a second time, the game time is over. When the gong is struck (by La Boule) the tigers are taken away by Monique, the gate to the Treasure Room rises and will only stay open for 2:00 minutes in UK series 1 to 4, the time stated did not include the 20 seconds before the gate started to rise or 3:00 minutes in UK series 5. The 3 minutes includes 20 seconds before the gate started to rise (to open canisters/organise team). The gate takes 30 seconds to open and close fully for every version of <i>Fort Boyard</i> worldwide.</p>
<p>The French version have extra games which are played in order to win extra time in the treasure room. Four or six members of the team play a game each against the "Master of Darkness", if they win they will be get extra time in the treasure room, making it a full 4 minutes. The starting time is 3:00 as normal, but the team must bet on the duels with this time. In 2012, the duels against the "Master of Darkness" could reduce the team's time to 2:15 (2:00 in 2011) and give them a maximum time of 3:45 (4:00 in 2011).</p>
<p>If by this time the team has still not figured out the password from the clues won, they can "sacrifice" players in exchange for extra clues to help them. The sacrificed players have to reach the clue by putting their hand into one of the tiger-shaped hand traps around the Treasure Room entrance; once their hands are inside they cannot release them and participate in collecting the gold.</p>
<p>The contestants now have to spell out the password on the giant alphabet on the floor of the treasure room by standing on the corresponding letters on the grid and using <a href="/wiki/Round_shot" title="Round shot">cannonballs</a> if there are not enough players. The team must also ensure the word is spelled correctly, as a mistake could cost them the prize.</p>
<p>Once this is done, Monique rotates the tiger's head (a statue), and the word will either be declared correct or incorrect, and the gold is released if the word is correct.</p>
<p>Then the contestants have the remaining time to collect as much gold as they can and place it in a bucket outside of the treasure room. It is only what is in this bucket that they get to keep; any that lands on the floor is not counted. When the time is nearly up in the treasure room, a bell rings, and the gate begins to close slowly. The contestants have to leave before the gate shuts completely because when the door shuts the tigers are released back into the treasure room. (the release of the tigers is delayed until the contestants are out of the treasure room, a portcullis is pulled in some versions to block the tigers from being released). In the 1990 French version,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and in the 2006 Russian version of the show, contestants were "locked" in the treasure room. On both occasions, the gold collected was lost as a result.</p>
<p>If, however, they declare an incorrect word, the gold is not released and instead the gate to the treasure room begins to close immediately, prompting the contestants to make a quick escape, and they complete the game with no winnings.</p>
<p>The won gold is then weighed and converted into currency; this makes the contestants’ prize money. In most countries, the money won by the team is given to a charity.</p>
<p>Some countries, including Spain, Argentina, the UK, and Belgium, give the money directly to the members of the team. Some give vacations instead of money, dependent on how much the team won.</p>
<p>In France, between 1990 and 1992, the treasure was given to the team, but since 1993, the whole prize goes to charity. Then again in 2010, the prize money was given to the contestants.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">Broadcast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Broadcast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK_transmissions">UK transmissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: UK transmissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In total, 57 episodes were shown in the original Channel 5 series; including four celebrity specials and a special edition with contestants from the first series of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mole_(UK_TV_series)" title="The Mole (UK TV series)">The Mole</a></i>.</p>
<p>On 1 July 2014, Challenge announced on social media that they had re-acquired all the Channel 5 years of the show (previously repeated by the channel from 2002–2006) and would begin airing series 1–2 in August that year, with series 3 and 4 following in 2015. Series 1 started on 4 August at 5pm, followed by series 2 on 18 August 2014. Series 3 starts on 7 May 2015 at 6pm.</p>
