<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_details">Technical details</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Technical details">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From a broadcasting perspective, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard_(fortification)" title="Fort Boyard (fortification)">Fort Boyard</a> itself was refurbished during 1988–89 to become, essentially, a large outdoor television studio. The Fort has its own doctor, catering facilities, as well as production gallery and veterinary centre.</p>
<p>The Fort is equipped with 10 portable television cameras, one camera crane for overhead shots, one under-water camera as well as a number of smaller cameras which specifically cover individual games and challenges around the Fort.</p>
<p>The majority of shows are filmed in the <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)#4:3_standard" title="Aspect ratio (image)">4:3</a> <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)" title="Aspect ratio (image)">aspect ratio</a>, although some shows, for countries including Sweden and France since 2008, now use the more common <a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">16:9</a> widescreen aspect ratio. <a href="/wiki/PAL" title="PAL">PAL</a> is the favoured recording format for <i>Fort Boyard</i>, offering the highest quality pictures. From 2013, the fort is now able to record programmes in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">HD</a> for the first time.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variations_to_the_format">Variations to the format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Variations to the format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1996, at the height of the French version's popularity, a mini-series entitled <i>Fort Boyard at Night</i> was shown in the autumn. It was filmed entirely at night, and the teams also had slightly more time in which to complete the challenges. In 1997, there were three night-time specials, at Halloween, Christmas, and New Year. In 2012, three further night-time editions were filmed and aired between Halloween and Christmas on 31 October, 22 December and 29 December.</p>
<p>In some of the French (Seasons 14–16, 2003–2005) and Russian versions (2003–2004), the contestants stay overnight in the Fortress. During this time, they played endurance, mind, and psychological games both for the release of any prisoners they may have had, and for keys to, or time in, the <i>Treasure Room</i> at the end of the game.</p>
<p>Although most seasons have seen changes (not least in hosts), recent changes to the <b>French version</b> of <i>Fort Boyard</i> included:</p>
<ul>
<li>From 2006 to 2009, the number of keys determined how much access the team had to the <i>Treasure Room</i>. 5 keys were the minimum needed to open the gate, but the gate would only open to a certain height, which made carrying coins through the gate difficult. A 6th key would open the gate roughly halfway, but it was still not easy to get through. To open the gate fully, 7 keys were needed. In 2006, when the host pulls the switch the <i>Treasure Room</i> gate would start to open immediately. If a team member did not get out of the <i>Treasure Room</i> in time, a portcullis was activated which stopped the tigers, but the money collected was lost forever.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Council">The Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: The Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In the council, teams no longer play to free prisoners; rather, they play for up to 60 extra seconds of extra time in the <i>Treasure Room</i>, in addition to the three minutes guaranteed. From 1995 to 2011, there were a total of 31 different council games.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Hall of Imprints</b></p>
<ul>
<li>There was a new section in which one member donned a diving suit and dived down to the underwater control centre. There, he or she was guided by the team through an underground passage filled with traps and coded doors towards the "Hall of Imprints", freeing their prisoners along the way. Once all members (except the diver) had reached the Hall, they used their right hands to release the crystal, which they needed to enter the council.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_season">2007 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 2007 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>They have extra games which are played in order to win extra time in The Treasure Room. Four members of the team play a game each against the Master of Darkness, if they won they got 15 seconds each, a total of 1 minute, of extra time in the Treasure room, making it a full 4 minutes.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Treasure Room</b></p>
<ul>
<li>2007 was the only season the time in the <i>Treasure Room</i> started at the opening of the gate. The team had 3:00–4:00 minutes from when the host pulled the switch to open the gate. The team also had 25 seconds (if they had 6 keys) or 15 seconds (if they had 7 keys) before the start of the time; this made the time actually 3:15–4:25 minutes in total.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_season">2008 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: 2008 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In 2008, the diving section changed. All members except the diver entered the control centre. They had to put 9 colored cubes in the correct order, using clues provided by the host. Once the 9 cubes are in place, the trap door for the diver opened. The diver entered a flooded room, with a treasure box, a drawing, and a maze with various colored keys in it. He or she has had to describe the small drawing to the other team members. The drawing corresponds to a drawing on one of the 9 colored cubes. The color of the matching cube determined the key to retrieve from the maze. The team members had to guide the diver through the maze, as the diver only see it from behind. After the key had been freed, it was used to unchain the treasure box. The box was then lifted from the water, but couldn't be opened yet. The key to open it was inside the <i>Treasure Room</i> and would fall down together with the gold.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_season">2009 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: 2009 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>2009 saw many more changes. Main changes included new opening titles, graphics and a <i>wall of progress</i> which Demi (Passe Muraille) was in control of which lined the wall of the Fort (the wall above the <i>Treasure Room</i>). There were 6 new key games and 2 new clue games in 2009.</p>
<ul>
<li>One of the first major changes on the Fort was the before game challenge, called <i><b>The Tube</b></i>, which was only used this season. There was a large tube full of coloured water. The team had to find 2 black scratching posts, situated around the Fort, to find the numbers which was the combination to unlock the box containing the cup which was connected to the tube . If they could fill the cup with water before the tube ran out they got a bonus key game after the 45:00 minutes of key games had finished. This game was played in the central circle before the gong.</li>
<li>Another change was that teams no longer stopped collecting keys at 7 keys but could continue on to collect up to 10 keys. These extra 3 keys were exchanged for clue words at the <i>Treasure Room</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Extra Games</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The middle section of the game was also different. There were now 3 boxes which contained money. The problem was that 2 of them were sealed with glass. During this the prisoners would play <i><a href="/wiki/Fear_Factor" title="Fear Factor">Fear Factor</a></i> style games in an attempt to win "pieces" to eliminate colours. The prisoners were released but if they did not win their games they were not allowed inside the <i>Treasure Room</i>.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Duels were different in 2009. The team could see what was happening through a window. The starting time was 3:00, but the team needed to bet on the duels with time. These times were <b>30 seconds</b>, <b>20 seconds</b>, <b>10 seconds</b>, and <b>−15 seconds</b>. If they win on −15 Seconds they did not lose any time. This made the minimum time in the <i>Treasure Room</i> 2:45, with the maximum being a full 4:00 minutes.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Treasure Room</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The <i>Treasure Room</i> had changed in 2009. Firstly, the 6 key sign was raised to shoulder height. Secondly, teams couldn't trade clues for extra keys; they had to play with the keys they had. (If they got under 5 keys someone was sacrificed to Mr. Chan to gain a key.) In the <i>Treasure Room</i> they collected keys for boxes containing extra gold. They were allowed to pick only one box, at the end, and were allowed as many keys as there were people in the <i>Treasure Room</i>. Picking the correct box earned the team the extra gold.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Duel_format">Duel format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Duel format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2004, a duel/tournament format has been used by other countries, who prefer this version of <i>Fort Boyard</i>. Two teams play in the Fort at the same time, with only one of them winning at the end. A similar format was used in 1991.</p>
<p>In 2007 and 2008, a formula with duels between three countries (Bulgaria, Serbia and Turkey) was used; two countries (Belgium and Netherlands) in 1991 and with teams of teenagers in 2011 (United Kingdom and United States).</p>
<p>Countries that have used this format include:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li>Azerbaijan (2013–14)</li>
<li>Belgium &amp; Netherlands (1991)</li>
<li>Balkins (Tri-nations of Bulgaria, Serbia and Turkey) (2007–08)</li>
<li>Bulgaria (2009)</li>
<li>Canada (2013–14)</li>
<li>Denmark (2009–2010)</li>
<li>Finland (2010, 2012)</li>
<li>France (2010)</li>
<li>Germany (2010)</li>
<li>Greece (2006–08)</li>
<li>Netherlands (2011–12, 2014)</li>
<li>Norway (2010–11)</li>
<li>Russia (2006, 2012)</li>
<li>Sweden (2004, 2010–)</li>
<li>United Kingdom (2011–14)</li>
<li>United States (1991 pilot, 2011)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="French_version">French version</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: French version">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2010, the duel format was introduced to the show following the low ratings for the previous season in 2009. Although, this was not successful in the French version and was later dropped the same year. The show returned to a more classical version in 2011.</p>
<p>The changes made to the French version in 2010 were:</p>
<p><b>Main overview</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Passe-Temps and Mr. Chan left the show.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olivier_Minne" title="Olivier Minne">Olivier Minne</a> became the only host.</li>
<li>Two teams competed to try to win the most keys in the first section.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Game Play</b></p>
<ul>
<li>12 teams of 4 play 2 sections of the game. The Special team play only section 2 in game of episode 1 because all 4 members are former contestants in <i>Fort Boyard</i>.</li>
<li>The team who won were called the "champion team" and would return the following week. Until the last episode, the Special team would play as the "normal team".</li>
<li>Key games not only included the ones inside cells but also the clue games, which were played against a clepsydre. If the team lost a clue game they were made prisoner.</li>
<li>There were 3 rounds of key games. Before each round there was a duel. Winning the duel not only won them a key, but also meant the other team had to win their game or their player was automatically made a prisoner.</li>
<li>If there is no clear winner after the 3 rounds a new section of the show, <i><b>Crossbow Relay</b></i>, was introduced. Before this, the prisoners were released. All members had to complete a relay course for keys.</li>
<li>The team with the lowest amount of keys was sent off the Fort and a new team (champion team from last week) was sent back to compete against the current champions.</li>
<li>The champion team from the last episode then faced the round 1 winners in clue games. These clue games can be key games with clue canisters, or clue games which were against the clepsydre.</li>
<li>There were 3 rounds of clue games, with each round starting with a duel. Again the losing team was made prisoner if they didn't win their clue game, but the winning team also got to choose which team got to play which game.</li>
<li>After the clue rounds, any prisoners were released by the duels in the council room. 2/3 was required to win.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Treasure Room</b></p>
<ul>
<li>At the <i>Treasure Room</i>, both teams used their clues and wrote down the codeword on a slate. Once this was put in place they had the remaining time of 3:30 (which included working out the code word). After 1 minute the gate started to open and began closes after 3:00 minutes (took 30 seconds to close fully). At around 0:15 seconds the slots were closed so the team couldn't insert any more money.</li>
<li>The gold was then weighed and the codes were revealed. The team with the highest gold and correct codeword won.</li>
<li>If both teams had the correct code, the team with the highest weight of gold won €10,000 and returned the following week.</li>
<li>If both teams had the incorrect code, the champion team would return the following week, but didn't win €10,000.</li>
<li>The team which won the Grand Final (episode 7) would receive €50,000 prize (includes the €10,000 won previously).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_German_changes">2010 German changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: 2010 German changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Most of the show's characters are gone.</li>
<li>The <i>Watch Tower</i> and the riddles have been removed.</li>
<li>The duel/tournament format was used.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_French_changes">2011 French changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: 2011 French changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Main overview</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Olivier Minne continues as the only host.</li>
<li>Return to a more "classic" format, one team and seven keys required. (45 mins of key games, 25 mins for the adventures)</li>
<li>Return of celebrities playing for charity.</li>
<li>3 new characters, including the return of the mud wrestler (Lady Boo).</li>
<li>Father Fouras now chairs the Council.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The team can see what is happening in the Council through a window. The starting time is 3:00, but the team must bet on the duels with this time. The times are <b>20 seconds</b>, <b>15 seconds</b>, <b>15 seconds</b> and <b>10 seconds</b>. If they win on their choosing time it will be added to the 3:00 minutes, but if they lose it will be deducted. This makes the minimum time in the <i>Treasure Room</i> 2:00, with the maximum being a full 4:00.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Hall Of Judgement</b></p>
<p>This takes place after the key games. <i>The Hall of Judgement</i> provides opportunities for candidates to obtain the missing keys against the sacrifice of one of them but also to free the team members locked in during the first half. The challenges are set by new female character, the <b>White Judge</b>; played by Louise-Marie Hustings in 2011, then Raphaëlle Lenoble during 2012, and <a href="/wiki/Delphine_Wespiser" title="Delphine Wespiser">Delphine Wespiser</a> since 2013 (who was a contestant at Halloween 2012). The challenges used are similar to those on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cube_(game_show)" title="The Cube (game show)">The Cube</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Minute_to_Win_It" title="Minute to Win It">Minute to Win It</a></i>.</p>
<ul>
<li>Each team member is free to be sacrificed to receive an extra key. The <i>White Judge</i>, sets a challenge the sacrifice/prisoner must complete in order to be released. If failed, they go directly into the terrible jails of <i>La Boule</i> until the end of the show; if they succeed, however, they are released and return to their team.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Treasure Room</b></p>
<ul>
<li>When the host pulls the switch, the <i>Treasure Room</i> gate will start to open immediately. This was also done in 2006.</li>
<li>The team have 12 seconds to process the password, instead of the normal 15 seconds.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_UK_changes">2011 UK changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: 2011 UK changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fort_Boyard:_Ultimate_Challenge" title="Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge">Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge</a></div>
<p><b>Main overview</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The show is now called <i>Fort Boyard: Ultimate Challenge</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Laura_Hamilton" title="Laura Hamilton">Laura Hamilton</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andy_Akinwolere" title="Andy Akinwolere">Andy Akinwolere</a>, previously <a href="/wiki/Geno_Segers" title="Geno Segers">Geno Segers</a>, present the new series.</li>
<li>Teams are made-up of teenagers aged between 13–19 years old.</li>
<li>The show's characters are gone and until series 4, the tigers were not used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>The teams only collect keys and the <i>Treasure Room</i> section is changed.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_French_changes">2012 French changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: 2012 French changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The times are <b>20 seconds</b>, <b>15 seconds</b> and <b>10 seconds</b>. If they win on their choosing time it will be added to the 3:00 minutes, but if they lose it will be deducted. This makes the minimum time in the <i>Treasure Room</i> 2:15, with the maximum being 3:45 if all bets are won. The second duel is now a word puzzle rather than a contest with the Master of Shadows.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_French_changes">2014 French changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: 2014 French changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>The times are <b>10 seconds</b> for three games and <b>30 seconds</b> for two games. If they win on their choosing time it will be added to the 3:00 minutes, but if they lose it will be deducted. This makes the minimum time in the <i>Treasure Room</i> 1:30, with the maximum being 4:30 if all bets are won. The prisoners will be released with 15 seconds deducted for each player.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_French_changes">2015 French changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: 2015 French changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>The Cage</b></p>
<ul>
<li>A new area was added, called The Cage. This happens at the 25 minute mark in part 1. The team must sacrifice 1 key to enter The Cage, where three of the team members will compete in individual games against one of the Fort's guards. Each challenge completed successfully adds a key to the team's total, meaning if all 3 team members win their games, the net profit is 2 keys.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Prisoner Escape</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Prisoners are now allowed to escape after Part 2, completing a course to get out of prison. The prisoner has 1:30 to escape, and any additional time taken is deducted from the team's starting 2:00 in the <i>Treasure Room</i>.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Duels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Duels no longer deduct from the team's <i>Treasure Room</i> time, they only add time depending on the team member's performance in the duel. This includes a new clock for Father Fouras' riddle, which is divided into three sections, 30, 20, and 10. Should the team member solve the riddle in time, the amount of time added is determined by the section the clock pointer is in, meaning the riddle is worth less time the longer it takes to solve it.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The music for the original French version of <i>Fort Boyard</i> was composed by <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Koulak" title="fr:Paul Koulak">Paul Koulak</a>, a French music <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a>. He composed the main themes for the show as well as the <a href="/wiki/Incidental_music" title="Incidental music">incidental music</a> and game music that is used throughout the show. His music has been used for every version of <i>Fort Boyard</i> around the world, except the German version, where they composed their own music for the show and games.</p>
<p>Up to 2014, six different opening theme songs have been used on the show; the first was used until 1994, the second in 1995, the third from 1996–2000, the fourth in 2001 and 2002 (used by the UK in 2003 during the Treasure Room), the "Dance Version" (used by France during the end credits of the night editions in 1996 and the UK from 1999 to 2001) and the current theme song which was introduced in the 2003 French version. <i>Fort Boyard Ultimate Challenge</i> uses a different opening theme and game music but does use the recent French opening credits and logo.</p>
<p>Some of the original music for <i>Fort Boyard</i> was released on CD in France, both on CD single and CD album form, in 1999. Tracks that featured on these CDs include:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Fort Boyard Main Title Theme</i></li>
<li><i>Fort Boyard Main Theme, Dance Version</i></li>
<li><i>March of the Tigers</i></li>
<li><i>The Cable Cycle</i></li>
<li><i>From One Point in the Course to Another</i></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Boyard:_Le_D.C3.A9fi"><i>Fort Boyard: Le Défi</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Fort Boyard: Le Défi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Fort Boyard: Le Défi</i> is a PC <a href="/wiki/CD-ROM" title="CD-ROM">CD-ROM</a> game based on the television show and released in 1995. It provides the player the possibility to become a team member, playing the well known game in the Fort. The game was created by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microids" title="Microids">Microids</a>, France Televisions and R&amp;P Electronic Media. The game was available in French and Dutch.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Boyard:_La_Legende"><i>Fort Boyard: La Legende</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fort_Boyard_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Fort Boyard: La Legende">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Fort Boyard: La Legende</i> is an action adventure game, based in and around La Rochelle and on <i>Fort Boyard</i>. It was only released in the original French version (as a sort of tie-in to the game show) and the later Dutch-spoken versions. The lack of an English version made this game highly obscure: it doesn't have a <a href="/wiki/MobyGames" title="MobyGames">MobyGames</a> entry. The hero of this game has no name; he is going to look for a treasure that was hidden by Napoleon at <i>Fort Boyard</i>. For this he needs to look around for clues, and get people to help, in and around <a href="/wiki/La_Rochelle" title="La Rochelle">La Rochelle</a>.</p>
<p>The game is quite short: one can finish it in two hours. One attempt to stretch it is by putting in a lot of points where the player has lost the game. For instance, if the player is rude to Liliane Denis in the bar, she will not help, so the player cannot finish the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Fort Boyard: La Legende</i> was released in 1996 by Expand Images, Microïds, <a href="/wiki/France_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9visions" title="France Télévisions">France Télévisions</a>, and R&amp;P Electronic Media.</p>
